<div id="review_1734825457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1734825457" />
    <a title="Cindy Newton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6082517-cindy-newton"><img alt="Cindy Newton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432075684p2/6082517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1734825457?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy Newton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy Newton" href="/user/show/6082517-cindy-newton">Cindy Newton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/23435901-weaveworld">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=audible">audible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1734825457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9552569454306113516">I enjoyed this story, although at times I wasn't sure. There were moments as I read this fantasy about another world, woven into a carpet, peopled with magical characters, that the line between fascination and skepticism would begin to blur, and I would feel doubt. My investment into the story would begin to recoil. This happened a couple of times at the beginning, and then again in the middle when the action would lull, but it passed quickly each time. <br/><br/>I found the fight to save the Fugue more i</span>
  <span id="freeText9552569454306113516" style="display:none">I enjoyed this story, although at times I wasn't sure. There were moments as I read this fantasy about another world, woven into a carpet, peopled with magical characters, that the line between fascination and skepticism would begin to blur, and I would feel doubt. My investment into the story would begin to recoil. This happened a couple of times at the beginning, and then again in the middle when the action would lull, but it passed quickly each time. <br /><br />I found the fight to save the Fugue more interesting than the Fugue itself, for the most part. I think the format of the audible book doesn't lend itself so well to deep analysis of a text--at least, not for me. I know, from looking at other reviews, that there is a lot of allusion, a lot of symbolism at play here, but when I'm just listening to a book, I tend to just let it wash over me without thinking of the deeper elements of the story. That's why I avoid classic lit on audio--I feel I would miss too much. <br /><br />I found the characters likable, although Cal and Suzanna took a little while to get up to speed on the dangers of their situations at the beginning. I especially enjoyed Shadwell and his smarmy, unctuous manner. The Hag and the Magdalene were also horrifically fascinating. Although I was slightly bored by the good times in the Fugue, I was saddened by the ultimate fate of some of these characters.<br /><br />All in all, it's an absorbing read (or listen!) which I recommend to fans of fantasy. The audio narrator is British, too, and that's always a plus in my book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9552569454306113516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_648952742" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648952742" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21577831-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584934953p2/21577831.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/648952742?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/21577831-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer648952742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1451896359449313890">*I decided to edit my review (from 4 stars to 5 stars) because after 2 years, I cannot get this book out of my head. It goes down in my life as one of the most memorable, intriguing, and stimulating books I have ever read. A must-read for Barker fans, or anyone who likes cross-genre books (horror, fantasy, action). Great book. Read below for my original review................<br/><br/>The best thing about this book is that it is able to cross genres seamlessly. With elements of fantasy, horror and science</span>
  <span id="freeText1451896359449313890" style="display:none">*I decided to edit my review (from 4 stars to 5 stars) because after 2 years, I cannot get this book out of my head. It goes down in my life as one of the most memorable, intriguing, and stimulating books I have ever read. A must-read for Barker fans, or anyone who likes cross-genre books (horror, fantasy, action). Great book. Read below for my original review................<br /><br />The best thing about this book is that it is able to cross genres seamlessly. With elements of fantasy, horror and science fiction, it has become my favorite "non-genre" that I will surely look for in other books. It has the best elements of these genres and seamlessly weaves them in together (see what I did there?). A true mind fuck.<br /><br />With such a strange and unique concept for the book, it had to be well written for the reader to understand and imagine what the hell is going on. Clive Barker did that: Weaveworld has great imagery, character development and is overall an EXCELLENT read. I would have given it 5 stars except...<br /><br />It is just too damn long. The version I bought has 648 pages and about 3/4 of the way through the story things get a little stagnant. Without spoiling anything, what started out as one main story line goes into several, so it takes a chapter for each story to have its moment. The result is a very long, drawn out 150 pages or so that could have better been shrunk down to 50 pages. <br /><br />Overall, I highly recommend this book to anyone who enjoys a mind fuck. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1451896359449313890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer11821142016533762824">Barker lets loose his imagination as he takes you on an unforgettable trip to fantastic and incredible worlds of pure fantasy. His writing style engrosses the reader deep within the pages, immersing you into a dark and wonderful land of the unbelievable. He takes you on a trip of the magical and macabre and celebrates the potential of the human imagination.<br/><br/>The novel will grip you from the start and keep you desperate to keep reading. It is a book of dark fantasy that leaves you breathless after </span>
  <span id="freeText11821142016533762824" style="display:none">Barker lets loose his imagination as he takes you on an unforgettable trip to fantastic and incredible worlds of pure fantasy. His writing style engrosses the reader deep within the pages, immersing you into a dark and wonderful land of the unbelievable. He takes you on a trip of the magical and macabre and celebrates the potential of the human imagination.<br /><br />The novel will grip you from the start and keep you desperate to keep reading. It is a book of dark fantasy that leaves you breathless after each page. First published back in 1987, the novel has remained one of the most talked about of Barker's books to date.<br /><br />With so many of Barker's novels, you can't help but wonder at the symbolism within the stories. The characters often reflect and resemble his ideas and views on his life and the society around him. This brings in a whole new level to the book, where one starts to interpret the messages and moral dilemmas within the pages.<br /><br />Weaveworld will leave your head spinning with thoughts and feelings once you finally put the book down, finished. It will teleport you slowly back to reality with a memory of the fantastic and magical. Nothing comes close to the escape of a novel of such talent and imagination. A book to love forever.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10817348004136491340">This is one of my very favorite books. I don't usually reread books, but I do with Weaveworld. It is so imaginative and fantastic - imagine the coolest, craziest rug you've ever seen. Then imagine that it's actually a world, whose magical inhabitants wove themselves into the rug to hide themselves from The Scourge, which seeks to destroy them.<br/><br/>A rather silly British fellow has a few of these magical people appear from a torn segment of the rug, and he's off on the most intense adventure...</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1243943849" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1243943849" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3403278-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604899399p2/3403278.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1243943849?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/3403278-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781554680924" href="/book/show/2767171-weaveworld">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3403278-michael?shelf=art">art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3403278-michael?shelf=aa-europelit">aa-europelit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3403278-michael?shelf=all-five-star">all-five-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3403278-michael?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3403278-michael?shelf=xlong-over-400">xlong-over-400</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3403278-michael?shelf=zz1987">zz1987</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3403278-michael?shelf=surrealism">surrealism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3403278-michael?shelf=aaa-favoritefiction">aaa-favoritefiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3403278-michael?shelf=aa-englandlit">aa-englandlit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3403278-michael?shelf=magicalrealism">magicalrealism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1243943849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14958907246450454355">290220: well i have not read any more barker to finish but perhaps that is so i do not become disappointed...<br/><br/>020515: this is a later addition: thinking about this some more. though i have many other works to read i will get to barker's 'imajica' soon, but then decided to rec this to all without edit my various e-friends on GR. this is not my usual literature nor philosophy. i did very much enjoy this. i hope this works for others...<br/><br/>first review: well. this novel, this world, this plot, all engag</span>
  <span id="freeText14958907246450454355" style="display:none">290220: well i have not read any more barker to finish but perhaps that is so i do not become disappointed...<br /><br />020515: this is a later addition: thinking about this some more. though i have many other works to read i will get to barker's 'imajica' soon, but then decided to rec this to all without edit my various e-friends on GR. this is not my usual literature nor philosophy. i did very much enjoy this. i hope this works for others...<br /><br />first review: well. this novel, this world, this plot, all engaged me far beyond what was expected. i have had this book, heard of this book, for some time- reading some of barker's books of blood did not encourage me- so there was no urgency, though as i look at it now, wonder what i would have thought of it had i read it years ago...<br /><br />would i have found, for example, thinking of all other mundane fantasies- tech, culture, politics, all medieval- such great pleasure that it is not that sort, would i have found it spurring my critical thoughts in a way mundane mundane lit almost never does- where what interests me most is how the story is told, not what the story is- would i have thought of the philosophical impression of this vivid strangeness, would i have thought of... Schopenhauer?<br /><br />this is an odd favourite, in some ways, as it is very long, is not uniquely told but rather transparently and openly as any non- genre writing. it does have some arresting images, likeable characters, understandable bad characters, lightly given metaphysics surrounding the magic weaves, the magic raptures, the mature love, fallible memories, prejudices, but none of this relies too much on say Christian worldview. i am not a particularly fast reader, i have read long books before but rarely search one out, i rarely find the pages slip by so quickly. on the other: i read this in one day, yes all 736 pages, in a few sittings, and my interest never flagged, my attention never wandered, so this must be some sort of rec. part of the pleasure of reading this was doubtless novelty and low expectations. now, i just might read it again, at a slower, more thoughtful pace...<br /><br />for this single long novel allowed me such pleasure, far beyond what gained in reading parts, never wholes, of the usual epic fantasy series. i understand barker is unique, though was rec'd lovecraft and Clark Ashton Smith, and in my reading was drawn to compare with Ben Okri, the Nigerian author just read, three books of the famished road series which are basically one long book divided in three. and of course Tolkien. and then Stephen King, an author whose fantasy works to which many friends direct me, but i enjoyed barker far more than anything by King. so this is once again reason to search out work i might never have heard of, i looked at, i searched for, as barker is not a lit award winner...<br /><br />that the world is magical beyond what we sense, is a common fantasy trope. that this need not be a universe starkly divided into capital G good and capital E evil- this is more mature, more interesting, and that this world, woven rug in our common world, is experienced through our ordinary-ish avatars, descendant of poet and descendant of witch, is much more involving than quests or use of magic or big sword. i had not expected this. i was pleasantly surprised. my day was otherwise empty yes, but i could have read something like this word count in three or four books rather than this one. it made me wonder, happily, how this would read to say the Nigerians who read Okri. it made me happy to discover another seam of precious fantasy metal that was not the familiar quasi-medieval, that had complex, real, sort of ordinary characters..,<br /><br />in recollection, after a day's thought, i smile thinking of that evil portal/character named primarily as a Salesman, i think of the coat of promises to be broken, desires captured only to be redoubled pain of losing, i think of the engendered children of the evil witch sisters, i think of the railroad train timetable and its fortuitous use, i think of the tantalizing glimpses of the woven world, the orchard of fruit you never get at the usual grocers, the horror of the very ground beneath your feet cracking open, all, all the surreal, the terrors and the delights, i think finally of how this our mundane world of snow, cold, blizzard, can only compound the fantastical horrors coming after us...<br /><br />so i guess i will try some more barker. someday return to this one. search perhaps fruitlessly for something similar...</span>
  <a data-text-id="14958907246450454355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119177877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3672109056430615390">Wow this is book to me was quite a disappointment. I found this book to be very long winded while at the same time it did not reveal much and left you wondering many questions. I found Cal to be a likable protagonist but did not care for Suzanne,the other main character. I felt the book should have ended at the three quarter mark where much of the main story lines were resolved. The last quarter of the book was painful to me as I no longer cared. I am giving this two stars even though I will pro</span>
  <span id="freeText3672109056430615390" style="display:none">Wow this is book to me was quite a disappointment. I found this book to be very long winded while at the same time it did not reveal much and left you wondering many questions. I found Cal to be a likable protagonist but did not care for Suzanne,the other main character. I felt the book should have ended at the three quarter mark where much of the main story lines were resolved. The last quarter of the book was painful to me as I no longer cared. I am giving this two stars even though I will probably look back at this one as less. If found this to be a long, drawn out story, that was not very detailed, and I never really found myself attached to the characters within. I cannot recommend this one, instead read one of Clive Barkers horror novels and be sure to watch all his movies!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3672109056430615390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rPG68AwxbegsXzv2eMhSLTlK+OVlZPXgmSAv/UdGiGQR3dtxbzTRek1pYE71un/nNkSQlt4fz8tq4BNIqLRydQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/10366.Clive_Barker">About Clive Barker</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/10366.Clive_Barker"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1430330407p3/10366.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/10366.Clive_Barker">Clive Barker
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
10,784
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11949302477910870873">Clive Barker was born in Liverpool, England, the son of Joan Rubie (née Revill), a painter and school welfare officer, and Leonard Barker, a personnel director for an industrial relations firm. Educated at Dovedale Primary School and Quarry Bank High School, he studied English and Philosophy at Liverpool University and his picture now hangs in the entrance hallway to the Philosophy Department. It </span>
  <span id="freeText11949302477910870873" style="display:none">Clive Barker was born in Liverpool, England, the son of Joan Rubie (née Revill), a painter and school welfare officer, and Leonard Barker, a personnel director for an industrial relations firm. Educated at Dovedale Primary School and Quarry Bank High School, he studied English and Philosophy at Liverpool University and his picture now hangs in the entrance hallway to the Philosophy Department. It was in Liverpool in 1975 that he met his first partner, John Gregson, with whom he lived until 1986. Barker's second long-term relationship, with photographer David Armstrong, ended in 2009.<br /><br />In 2003, Clive Barker received The Davidson/Valentini Award at the 15th GLAAD Media Awards. This award is presented "to an openly lesbian, gay, bisexual or transgender individual who has made a significant difference in promoting equal rights for any of those communities". While Barker is critical of organized religion, he has stated that he is a believer in both God and the afterlife, and that the Bible influences his work.<br /><br />Fans have noticed of late that Barker's voice has become gravelly and coarse. He says in a December 2008 online interview that this is due to polyps in his throat which were so severe that a doctor told him he was taking in ten percent of the air he was supposed to have been getting. He has had two surgeries to remove them and believes his resultant voice is an improvement over how it was prior to the surgeries. He said he did not have cancer and has given up cigars. On August 27, 2010, Barker underwent surgery yet again to remove new polyp growths from his throat. In early February 2012 Barker fell into a coma after a dentist visit led to blood poisoning. Barker remained in a coma for eleven days but eventually came out of it. Fans were notified on his Twitter page about some of the experience and that Barker was recovering after the ordeal, but left with many strange visions.<br /><br />Barker is one of the leading authors of contemporary horror/fantasy, writing in the horror genre early in his career, mostly in the form of short stories (collected in Books of Blood 1 – 6), and the Faustian novel The Damnation Game (1985). Later he moved towards modern-day fantasy and urban fantasy with horror elements in Weaveworld (1987), The Great and Secret Show (1989), the world-spanning Imajica (1991) and Sacrament (1996), bringing in the deeper, richer concepts of reality, the nature of the mind and dreams, and the power of words and memories.<br /><br />Barker has a keen interest in movie production, although his films have received mixed receptions. He wrote the screenplays for Underworld (aka Transmutations – 1985) and Rawhead Rex (1986), both directed by George Pavlou. Displeased by how his material was handled, he moved to directing with Hellraiser (1987), based on his novella The Hellbound Heart. His early movies, the shorts The Forbidden and Salome, are experimental art movies with surrealist elements, which have been re-released together to moderate critical acclaim. After his film Nightbreed (Cabal), which was widely considered to be a flop, Barker returned to write and direct Lord of Illusions. Barker was an executive producer of the film Gods and Monsters, which received major critical acclaim.<br /><br />Barker is a prolific visual artist working in a variety of media, often illustrating his own books. His paintings have been seen first on the covers of his official fan club magazine, Dread, published by Fantaco in the early Nineties, as well on the covers of the collections of his plays, Incarnations (1995) and Forms of Heaven (1996), as well as on the second printing of the original UK publications of his Books of Blood series.<br /><br />A longtime comics fan, Barker achieved his dream of publishing his own superhero books when Marvel Comics launched the Razorline imprint in 1993. Based on detailed premises, titles and lead characters he created specifically for this, the four interrelated titles — set outside the Marvel universe — were Ectokid,</span>
  <a data-text-id="11949302477910870873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
